<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_77dfe93d-ad4a-49f0-aa65-827fa00af068'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer5140431638123337762"><i>They killed my mother.<br/>They took our magic.<br/>They tried to bury us.<br/><br/><b>Now we rise.</b></i><br/><br/>Zélie Adebola remembers when the soil of Orïsha hummed with magic. Burners ignited flames, Tiders beckoned waves, and Zélie’s Reaper mother summoned forth souls.<br/><br/>But everything changed the night magic disappeared. Under the orders of a ruthless king, maji were killed, leaving Zélie without a mother </span>
  <span id="freeText5140431638123337762" style="display:none"><i>They killed my mother.<br />They took our magic.<br />They tried to bury us.<br /><br /><b>Now we rise.</b></i><br /><br />Zélie Adebola remembers when the soil of Orïsha hummed with magic. Burners ignited flames, Tiders beckoned waves, and Zélie’s Reaper mother summoned forth souls.<br /><br />But everything changed the night magic disappeared. Under the orders of a ruthless king, maji were killed, leaving Zélie without a mother and her people without hope.<br /><br />Now Zélie has one chance to bring back magic and strike against the monarchy. With the help of a rogue princess, Zélie must outwit and outrun the crown prince, who is hell-bent on eradicating magic for good.<br /><br />Danger lurks in Orïsha, where snow leoponaires prowl and vengeful spirits wait in the waters. Yet the greatest danger may be Zélie herself as she struggles to control her powers and her growing feelings for an enemy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5140431638123337762" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_36273872').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_36273872').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});

    <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell"><img alt="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584062476p2/2190064.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2319382893?book_show_action=true">Mar 31, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell">Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2319382893" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3806583788508150825"><a href='http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/alwaysbeebooked/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/> <br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1557712859i/27497283.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/><br/><b>Note: <u>I'm going to start blocking people who come onto this review to tell me that I have read or reviewed it incorrectly.</u> I tried it, I didn't like it, I wrote about my feelings. What do you want? A five-star review? Write your own. 😊<br/><br/><br/><br/>Note Pt. 2: Seriously. I don't want to argue with you dissenters about MY opinion. I was honest about how I felt. End. Of. Story. If you're going to come on here to argue with me about something in this re</b></span>
  <span id="freeText3806583788508150825" style="display:none"><a href="http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/alwaysbeebooked/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1557712859i/27497283.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br><b>Note: <u>I'm going to start blocking people who come onto this review to tell me that I have read or reviewed it incorrectly.</u> I tried it, I didn't like it, I wrote about my feelings. What do you want? A five-star review? Write your own. 😊<br><br><br><br>Note Pt. 2: Seriously. I don't want to argue with you dissenters about MY opinion. I was honest about how I felt. End. Of. Story. If you're going to come on here to argue with me about something in this review, you had better 1) be civil and 2) be sure to read ALL the comments first. You might think you're the first to tell me how I read this book wrong and why, but I can assure you, you're not. And I'm going to be exponentially much less patient with you than I was with the 23434343 people before you who felt similarly entitled, especially if you insult me.</b><br><br><br>After reading some of the five-star reviews for this book, I'm reevaluating how much I trust some of my friends. This was a <i>terrible </i>book. I don't think I've been this disappointed since picking up <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2018240965" rel="nofollow noopener">FLAME IN THE MIST</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2265538041" rel="nofollow noopener">THRONE OF GLASS</a>. What the hell were you guys reading? Is there a "good" version and a "shitty" version? What happened?<br><br><br><br>I specifically <i>chose </i>to read CHILDREN OF BLOOD AND BONE after <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2339361297" rel="nofollow noopener">AMERICANAH</a> because I thought they would complement each other well and lead to some interesting parallels that I could discuss in my review. AMERICANAH is a book that discusses the racial and cultural issues of real-life Nigeria, and CHILDREN OF BLOOD AND BONE is a book that discusses racial and cultural issues of a fantasy-inspired country <i>based </i>on Nigeria. I <i>loved </i>AMERICANAH and I was so sure that I would love CHILDREN OF BLOOD AND BONE because it's exactly what so many readers have been asking for: Diverse Fantasy!<br><br><br><br>CHILDREN OF BLOOD AND BONE is a fantasy novel inspired by Nigerian mythology, specifically focusing on the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orisha" rel="nofollow noopener">Orisha</a>. In this world, magic is forbidden and those who are descended from the maji are called "maggots" and systematically oppressed, if not killed outright. It's narrated by three characters, Zelie, who is a maji and a target of these genocidal tactics employed by their ruler, and also Inan and his sister, whose name I can't remember, who are the children of the evil king, but also maji, so uh-oh, nobody better find out or anything because that would be awkward.<br><br><br><br>Zelie runs away, accompanied by that sister, and Inan hunts them down while fighting his unwanted (of course) attraction to her. Because he can see her in <i>dreams</i>. *eye roll* All the people saying this book is action-packed must either never read <i>good </i>fantasy, are reading a completely different edition from mine, or are lying outright, because this was the LONGEST 500-something pages I've ever read BECAUSE IT'S SO SLOW-PACED, OMG. I didn't care about any of the characters. When the climax happens, we're supposed to be <i>so worried </i>for poor Zelie, but I didn't care because her voice is completely interchangeable with the other two. Characters appear whenever it's convenient for the plot, and there's a romance thrown in haphazardly because what's a YA without mediocre romance?<br><br><br><br>Because that's what this is. Just another generic fantasy story with cardboard cut-out characters and a tepid romance that lacks chemistry. The only thing that sets it apart is the setting and mythology. <br><br><br><br>I want to close with these thoughts. I get why so many people are excited about this book. It's thrilling to read books about people who are like you and have a narrative that you identify with. I emphasized that (more nicely) in my review of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2329088933" rel="nofollow noopener">TYLER JOHNSON WAS HERE</a>. Even if I thought it was a bad book, I can appreciate the meaning and importance it has for people who are seeking out those stories. Fantasy novels are notorious for having bad rep, and when you <i>do </i>see characters of color, they often fit neatly under the cringe-worthy <a href="http://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/MagicalNegro" rel="nofollow noopener">Magical Negro</a> umbrella, which is not cool. That's a huge reason behind why I was so ready to embrace this book: I want those diverse stories too. Stories that give a new perspective and delve into territories that aren't explored nearly enough.<br><br><br><br>However, I have seen people on Tumblr and Goodreads posting status updates about how they don't think people should be allowed to write negative reviews for diverse books because the intentions of the author supersede the quality of the writing itself. I am 100% NOT OKAY with that, and here's why: if you do that, you're going to create a culture of mediocrity, where people will feel comfortable churning out poor-quality books while using diversity the way you might use a checklist. I'm not saying that TYLER JOHNSON and CHILDREN OF BLOOD AND BONE fall into that category, but by shutting down valid criticism and enabling poor story-telling, this is going to be a problem.<br><br><br><br>Part of me kind of wondered if the publication of CHILDREN OF BLOOD AND BONE may have been rushed so the release date coincided with that of <i>Black Panther</i>. That could explain some of the problems. I wondered the same thing about CARVE THE MARK (a book that was seemingly inspired by Star Wars) and the closeness of its release date to <i>Rogue One</i>. For reference, CARVE THE MARK was published January 17, 2017 and <i>Rogue One </i>was released on December 10, 2016. Likewise, <i>Black Panther </i>came out on February 16, 2018 and CHILDREN OF BLOOD AND BONE was published on March 6, 2018. From a marketing perspective, it's a brilliant move, but a rushed release date could explain some of the pacing issues and the not-so-great writing.<br><br><br><br>I apologize if this seems harsh, but I am a book blogger who has <i>always </i>tried to be 100% honest even if that opinion is not popular. I have had people tell me that they will or won't buy books based on my reviews because they know I won't deceive them or sugar-coat. I rate on a purely entertainment-based rubric and don't take things like literary merit or the author's intentions into account. CHILDREN OF BLOOD AND BONE had wonderful intentions... but I thought it was a really sloppy, generic fantasy novel, and I am rating it as such. Maybe you'll get the "good" version everyone's raving about. ;-)<br><br><br><br>1 star</span>

<div id="review_2399306736" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2399306736" />
    <a title="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68538597-booksofradiance"><img alt="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513125058p2/68538597.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2399306736?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" href="/user/show/68538597-booksofradiance">❄️BooksofRadiance❄️</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68538597-booksofradiance?shelf=ya-fantasy-sci-fi">ya-fantasy-sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2399306736" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6926595714332600781"><b>An oversimplified extra-tropey YA on steroids.</b><br/><br/>Hmm, where does one begin?<br/><br/>Sooo, does the book that made headlines well before it was even published live up to its hype? It truly saddens me to say this but unfortunately, no. It absolutely does not and I’m pretty certain I’m in the minority.<br/><br/>At its core, this book was supposed to be about Institutional racism and oppression so I loved the message it was trying to relay but I hated the execution. What could have been an epic fantasy was ruined by its </span>
  <span id="freeText6926595714332600781" style="display:none"><b>An oversimplified extra-tropey YA on steroids.</b><br><br>Hmm, where does one begin?<br><br>Sooo, does the book that made headlines well before it was even published live up to its hype? It truly saddens me to say this but unfortunately, no. It absolutely does not and I’m pretty certain I’m in the minority.<br><br>At its core, this book was supposed to be about Institutional racism and oppression so I loved the message it was trying to relay but I hated the execution. What could have been an epic fantasy was ruined by its poor writing, immature characters, repetitive and cringy passages and incredibly inconsistent pacing. <br>In fact, the longer time passes and the more I think about it, the angrier I get. <br><br>I loved the west African setting and the overall point of the story, had it been written in a manner that had depth to it would’ve touched a chord with me. Explorations of social power, the deft portrayal of racial tensions and persecution, the prejudice and structural inequalities that resonate with our own world/time, all of which should have been enough for me to give this all the star rating in the world but I had so many other issues with it that I found too hard to overlook.<br><br>Let’s put aside the overly recycled plot and start with my three biggest problems: the romance, the magic system and the characters. <br><br>- The magic wasn’t as firmly defined as I would’ve liked and there were so many inconsistencies and discrepancies there. <br>It was written as if I was expected to know everything as to the machinations without any explanations whatsoever. None. Just throw in some elemental magic BS and voilà. Call it a day. <br><br>- The characters, however... oh, the characters. The gift that kept on giving. On and on and on for over 500 pages. 🤦‍♀️ <br>Probably the biggest downfall of this novel (and there are many). They’re so painfully bad they’re in the league of their own badness. <br>Save for Tzain, Zalie’s brother, I didn’t like any of them, or I did at the start and all went downhill toward the end. So many of their childish and immature actions kept pulling me out of the story and at a certain point it became too hard to enjoy the book for what it was, especially where Zélie was concerned. I mean, how immature and STUPID could a 16/17 year-old be? <br>And that sentence she kept repeating: <b>
  <i>’I let out a breath I didn’t know I was holding.’</i>
</b> I just... how do I even express my rage??<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1476111025ra/20803103.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>I hated the romance. I HATED IT. It was incredibly unnecessary, overly contrived and it blossomed literally in a matter of hours……..HOURS, people.</b><br>It wasn’t just that it was the definition of insta-love, it was also… so uncomfortable to read about and I found myself continualy fuming at what I was reading, screaming at the book: how do you not… how does this not….!! (spoilers). Not to mention cringing at every turn. <br><br>Inan, though his POV was my favourite out of the three, his character was aggravating to say the least. His indecisiveness, his murky sense of logic and the way he’d decide on one thing then change his mind literally the next page (over and over and over again) was…..oh so tiring. <br>Overall, his state of change was too abrubt to be believable and very, you guessed it, inconsistent. <br>		<br>Yet another problem I had was Amari’s unnecessary chapters. She spends the vast majority of the book accompanying Zélie, therefore making her chapters so overly repetitive. <br>The two narrating characters were restating their motivations and rehashing events that happened just pages before.<br>I love multi-perspective fantasy books but a multiple narrators technique only works well when characters are in different places or doing very different things and TELLING US DIFFERENT THINGS. <br><br>And last but certainly not least, the ending. I mean, what the bloody f was that? Obviously I can’t go into details so as not to spoil anything but to say I was extremely aggravated at the events that lead up to the ending would be a gross understatement. <br>It felt like certain things that a certain character did were so irritatingly and utterly dumb and completely out of left field that one could literally sum up the entire ending with: THE FUCK!? THIS!? THIS IS THE EPIC CONCLUSION WITH WHICH ONE IS REWARDED AFTER ENDURING A GRUELLING 500+ PAGES OF HORNY, TEMPERAMENTAL TEENAGERS?? 🥶<br>Not to mention you could tell from a mile away that everything was done for no other reason than a simple shock value which, by the way, wasn’t even that shocking since it was too busy being so embarrassingly stupid. <br>Couldn’t there have been a better way? None at all??<br><br>All in all, honestly, I don’t even know. I’m no stranger to failed expectations when it comes to overly hyped books but the sting of this particular disappointment... ah, what’s the point. I’m out. <br><br><br>Buddy read with Yusra💓</span>
  <a data-text-id="6926595714332600781" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2271349153" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2271349153" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2271349153?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2271349153" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3419360017219007186"><blockquote>
  <i>“No matter how much I crave peace, the gods have other plans.”</i>
</blockquote><br/>4 1/2 stars. Wow, I have had quite a week. I started <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34728667.Children_of_Blood_and_Bone__Legacy_of_Or_sha___1_' title='Children of Blood and Bone (Legacy of Orïsha, #1) by Tomi Adeyemi' rel='nofollow noopener'>Children of Blood and Bone</a> last Thursday as I was going into labour (because, why not?). Normally, I would devour a book like this in a day or two, but those of you with kids will know that's just not going to happen with a newborn. <br/><br/>Instead, this book rode with me through the hospital stay, sleepless nights, and postpartum weepies. It kept my eyes open on those long, long nights</span>
  <span id="freeText3419360017219007186" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“No matter how much I crave peace, the gods have other plans.”</i>
</blockquote><br />4 1/2 stars. Wow, I have had quite a week. I started <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34728667.Children_of_Blood_and_Bone__Legacy_of_Or_sha___1_" title="Children of Blood and Bone (Legacy of Orïsha, #1) by Tomi Adeyemi" rel="nofollow noopener">Children of Blood and Bone</a> last Thursday as I was going into labour (because, why not?). Normally, I would devour a book like this in a day or two, but those of you with kids will know that's just not going to happen with a newborn. <br /><br />Instead, this book rode with me through the hospital stay, sleepless nights, and postpartum weepies. It kept my eyes open on those long, long nights. It picked me up and threw me into another world of action and magic right when I needed it. All I can say is: Thank you, Ms Adeyemi.<br /><br />Oh okay, that's not <i>all</i> I can say. Though hopefully I don't sound too delirious.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34728667.Children_of_Blood_and_Bone__Legacy_of_Or_sha___1_" title="Children of Blood and Bone (Legacy of Orïsha, #1) by Tomi Adeyemi" rel="nofollow noopener">Children of Blood and Bone</a> is a West-African inspired fantasy set in the fictional land of Orïsha. It takes all the best bits of YA fantasy - princesses, tormented soldiers, the battle to restore magic vs suppress it - and does something completely new with these familiar elements. At its core, it's an <b>action-packed, fast-paced adventure</b> to restore magic to the world and complete a ritual before the approaching solstice is over and magic is lost forever.<br /><br />Beneath that, though, there are many darker themes. <b>The plot is intense and steeped in racially-charged violence</b>. Adeyemi draws many parallels with our own world, forcing the reader to pause and consider systemic racism and injustice in prison systems. And Zélie remembers the genocide executed on King Saran's orders all too well. The "Raid", as it is known, took her mother from her. Now, Zélie is a divîner - a maji without magic, though her abilities lie dormant, waiting for the missing scroll that can return her power.<br /><br />The book is told from alternating perspectives. One is Zélie, another is Princess Amari who Zélie reluctantly saves from the King's men, and the third is Amara's brother, Inan, who is sent to chase down and stop his sister and Zélie. With complex characters who naturally change and grow as the story progresses, I was hooked. I cared what happened to all three of them. There was never a boring moment. <br /><br />It is always risky to step into a book as hyped as this one, but I, for one, think it very much deserves it. A compelling, exciting plot, a completely non-white cast of characters, AND a thoughtful consideration of race, skin colour, and prejudice... impressive, to say the least. Though that cliffhanger is EVIL. How will we cope until the next book?<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3419360017219007186" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2293828292" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2293828292" />
    <a title="Emma Giordano" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano"><img alt="Emma Giordano" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569693958p2/30604861.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2293828292?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Giordano" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Giordano" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano">Emma Giordano</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2293828292" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5134051202757456423">5 STARS! This is genuinely the greatest debut fantasy novel, greatest fantasy novel in general that I have read in a very long time. Initially, I was TERRIFIED to read <i>Children of Blood and Bone</i>. The combination of it’s size and an epic high fantasy novel was very daunting to me, but I am so happy I picked it up. I cannot possibly recommend it enough.<br/><br/>The writing was fantastic. Despite being such a large novel, the pacing was well-done, where I felt I was flying through the novel much quicker tha</span>
  <span id="freeText5134051202757456423" style="display:none">5 STARS! This is genuinely the greatest debut fantasy novel, greatest fantasy novel in general that I have read in a very long time. Initially, I was TERRIFIED to read <i>Children of Blood and Bone</i>. The combination of it’s size and an epic high fantasy novel was very daunting to me, but I am so happy I picked it up. I cannot possibly recommend it enough.<br /><br />The writing was fantastic. Despite being such a large novel, the pacing was well-done, where I felt I was flying through the novel much quicker than many other long fantasy novels. Adeyemi has a beautiful prose that compliments such a vibrant world and mystical magic system. All elements of Orisha were flawlessly executed – the history, the divide among maji/diviners vs. nobles, the different types of magic, ALL OF IT. I’m totally infatuated with this world and cannot wait to see it expand in following novels.<br /><br />I really loved the characters in this story. Zelie is such a fierce warrior. I loved watching her strength grow, but also still preserving some of her innocence and vulnerability. I feel that she is such a wonderful protagonist that so many will fall in love with. Amari is another character I LOVE. Her character transformation was really well done. It was so nice to see a girl start out meek and afraid but slowly grow into herself and become more comfortable in a group of people totally different from her. I also find the friendship that develops between Zelie and Amari to be so sweet. They are so different and would not get along at an eye's glance, but I enjoyed watching them grow to support each other. Inan is a character I also loved, but I did have some issues with. I loved him as the vengeful prince out to prevent Zelie and Amari from bringing magic back. he was a GREAT villain to follow from the beginning with a ton of layers, and it was especially cool to follow the antagonist's perspective for once in YA. But as the story progresses and the characters go through new things, I found his characterization to be a bit off-putting. Inan is a very intense character to begin with and his changes are equally drastic. To keep it spoiler-free, there were some times where I felt his feelings and reactions just didn't make sense and flipped around a lot. I do still love him as much as the others, and I am definitely anticipating seeing more from this epic cast in the future.<br /><br />There is so much action in this story. There are endless chase scenes, epic battles using swords, staffs, bows, and different kinds of magic. There are unexpected twists and turns and just so much intensity. The plot is wonderfully constructed with so much to enjoy. <i>Children of Blood and Bone</i> will totally keep you on the edge of your seat the entire time while reading - but you won't be able to *completely* predict what's coming next.<br /><br />I'm completely obsessed with <i>Children of Blood and Bone</i>. My favorite new-to-me start to a fantasy saga. Surely, one of my favorites of the year. This book has gotten so much hype even before it's publication, and it is totally deserving of every ounce of it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5134051202757456423" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2679436163" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2679436163" />
    <a title=" Teodora " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69603149-teodora"><img alt=" Teodora " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582144281p2/69603149.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2679436163?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Teodora " class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Teodora " href="/user/show/69603149-teodora"> Teodora </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=on-app">on-app</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2679436163" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17426187580059008527">5/5 ⭐<br/><br/><b>Full review on my Blog:</b> <a href='https://thedacianshewolf.home.blog/2019/04/12/children-of-blood-and-bone-legacy-of-orisha-1-by-tomi-adeyemi/' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Dacian She-Wolf</a> 🐺<br/><br/>Let’s start with the basics: I am <b>*in love*</b> with the cover! Like, for real. Just look at it. It’s gorgeous. Lit. So pleasing to look at.<br/><br/>Okay, moving on. How much, on a scale of 1 to 10 do I love a good old dark mysticism story? The correct answer is 11. I do love this stuff. But it has to be really good. And the one expanded in <b>Children of Blood and Bone</b> is actually excitingly good. The book is part of the Legacy of Orïsha trilogy, so I am expect</span>
  <span id="freeText17426187580059008527" style="display:none">5/5 ⭐<br /><br /><b>Full review on my Blog:</b> <a href="https://thedacianshewolf.home.blog/2019/04/12/children-of-blood-and-bone-legacy-of-orisha-1-by-tomi-adeyemi/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dacian She-Wolf</a> 🐺<br /><br />Let’s start with the basics: I am <b>*in love*</b> with the cover! Like, for real. Just look at it. It’s gorgeous. Lit. So pleasing to look at.<br /><br />Okay, moving on. How much, on a scale of 1 to 10 do I love a good old dark mysticism story? The correct answer is 11. I do love this stuff. But it has to be really good. And the one expanded in <b>Children of Blood and Bone</b> is actually excitingly good. The book is part of the Legacy of Orïsha trilogy, so I am expecting more and better!<br /><br />I grew up surrounded by mysticism. I read folkloric tales about magical objects and miraculous heroes, about death and life, about mythical creatures, I heard stories from old men and women about horrifying exorcism acts and bloody rituals, I grew up believing my grandmother can do spells and her mother was, indeed, a witch, believing in the fabulous healing powers of herbs and cures and in every sinister curse and paranormal story I heard. This book just feeds my childhood lost stories and pets them on the head. I know, I’m macabre to think of that, but when you grow up with such things you don’t consider them that bad, but kind of normal. Like a legacy.<br /><br />The book starts in a powerful note, almost like a scream: Zélie, the protagonist, remembers with pain in her heart and mind how her <i>Mama</i> was being taken away by the King’s guards and killed in front of everyone with other <i>majis</i>. Eleven years in the future, Zélie grows up in a <i>magicless</i> environment, even though she has in her the seed of magic. The people like her, the children of the once killed majis are called <i>divîners</i> and they are considered the no-ones of the land of magicless (yes, this made-up word again!) Orïsha. <br /><br />Besides the interesting Nigerian mythology, the Yoruba belief, around which the book seems to revolve, another interesting path to follow is the development of the characters and how their faith changes. Of course, there is going to be a star-crossed love story, which for many of you might seem a bit off, but for me, it was just part of the unforgivable process of breaking my heart! Yes, the story gets more and more intense as you devour the pages with your all five senses, making your heartache and your mouth go crazy with uncontrollable words of surprise. Everything that seemed normal at the beginning is turned around at the end, nothing is what it was supposed to be. <b>„Let feeling become your eyes”</b> Zélie says, and this is exactly how you are going to get through this book. <i>Feeling</i> it.<br /><br />The most interesting character of all is, however, the persona of Amari. If she’s going to think forever at sweets and foods, then you know I can relate more than anything to her. She’s my type of girl! But, for real now, her development is truly amazing. She enters the scene by being a shy little princess, too afraid to even breath wrong in front of anyone, and she ends the first part of the story by gaining depth, power and knowledge. <br /><br />Behind all this fantastic story, however, an ugly truth is being hidden: the oppression is real. It is happening in the world we are all living in, it is affecting real people with real feelings. So this book is, also, an awakening call for humanity. <br /><br /><b>„I won’t let your ignorance silence my pain”</b>. A real pain that is beard by real people. Tomi Adeyemi feels deeply in her bones the pain of her nation and she is willing to share a bit of it with us, making the whole amount of her readers her own Connectors. <br /><br />From this book, as from any book that has ever been written, we have to learn something. And from this particular one, I’ve learned that no matter what, we have to fight for what we believe in because there is always a way. <br /><br /><b>„We are our own people. We make our own choices”.</b> Yes, indeed. But for that, we have to open our eyes and let our feelings flow.<br /><br /><br />(<a href="https://urcdn.eu/styles/15bb3fab-b685-423e-9b5d-7b2260ed09c6_original?b" rel="nofollow noopener">Book-inspired</a>)</span>
  <a data-text-id="17426187580059008527" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2306353733" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2306353733" />
    <a title="Ojo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19114590-ojo"><img alt="Ojo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521760904p2/19114590.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2306353733?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ojo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ojo" href="/user/show/19114590-ojo">Ojo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2306353733" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5032494971786635116">Mixed feelings, this one. <br/><br/>While it's a good book (for most YA fans), I found it far too typical, too clichéd, too predictable. <br/><br/>The book has spawned a lot of awesome reviews. For a debut novel, Tomi Adeyemi has actually done quite well. The writing style is especially good. But then, most of the good reviews garnered by this book are from Americans and Europeans, not Africans (especially Nigerians). She has the right idea, blending Yoruba mythology with regular YA. It's a great idea, but I must s</span>
  <span id="freeText5032494971786635116" style="display:none">Mixed feelings, this one. <br /><br />While it's a good book (for most YA fans), I found it far too typical, too clichéd, too predictable. <br /><br />The book has spawned a lot of awesome reviews. For a debut novel, Tomi Adeyemi has actually done quite well. The writing style is especially good. But then, most of the good reviews garnered by this book are from Americans and Europeans, not Africans (especially Nigerians). She has the right idea, blending Yoruba mythology with regular YA. It's a great idea, but I must say (from a Nigerian POV), it's poorly, poorly done. <br /><br />I was surprised to see that the book came with a map. Being a lover of maps, I was quite excited to see how the world-building would go. Alas, it turned out terribly sub-par. She tried uswd actual places in Nigeria as setting. While it's not a totally bad idea, the way she depicted the entire thing was thoroughly unsatisfying. A walled Lagos? Snow-capped mountains in Ibadan? A floating Ilorin? Really???<br /><br />And then there's the naming system. While you white folks are probably raving about the story and all, it's us Yoruba people that'll shake our heads at how our dear language was properly murdered. I felt the names were totally inappropriate. Yoruba is unlike the shallow English Language. It is a language with a lot of empahasis on semantics. Everything has a meaning. Every meaning, every name is significant. Funmilayo Forest??? Really??? How is a forest supposed to give you joy??? Forests in Yoruba mythology are dark, forbidden places, typically evil in nature. We don't use 'wood' or 'jungle' to describe them in Nigeria. It's just not appropriate. They're called 'forest' because that's the closest word in the English Language that indicate a bit of their mytho-religious significance. Adetunji Sea? Really? In short, I felt the names didn't reflect the soul of what they were meant to represent. Mines of Calabrar? That's straight from Legend of the Seeker. She could've simply said Calabar. When Calabar is discussed, what comes to mind is the beautiful women and the delicious food. I don't think there are any mines in Calabar. Perhaps, a floating Calabar would've been more appropriate instead of a floating Ilorin. <br /><br />The summary is that I felt Tomi tried to compress African setting and mytho-religion into the narrow confines of American YA. While the writing and the storyline are quite good, it's the world-building that's the problem. I'd score it a big zero and I'm sure any Nigerian who comes across this will definitely feel the same. <br /><br />The book appeals to white folk because it's written to resemble American YA. The gods and goddesses of Yoruba traditional religion are not as nice, not as approachable and certainly darker. <br /><br />The use of the Yoruba language in the books is pretty much unsatisfactory. Incantations are certainly not that literal. Real incantations are composed of a complex kind of poetry in mostly archaic Yoruba, a lot of figurative meanings, allusions and other indirect literary devices. <br /><br />It's not a bad book altogether though. But it's not 100% African. It's a supposedly African book that closely mirrors American YA. Maybe 5% African. The soul of the entire thing is certainly not African, and definitely not Yoruba. <br /><br />If you're looking for an enjoyable YA read with sweet characters, then this book is for you. But if you're Nigerian and you're hoping to find something of our culture in this, chances are you'd be disappointed. <br /><br />I'm focusing on the poorer side of this read because I'm Yoruba, and I was excited to see some proper employment of Yoruba mythology in fantasy writing. Hopefully the next book in the series will come with big improvements in the world-building because I'm certainly going to read it. <br /><br />Thumbs up to the author nonetheless.<br /><br />3/1/20<br />Below is the GR link to my review of book 2. Be interested in reading thoughts on that as well <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3073459826?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5032494971786635116" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2338644720" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2338644720" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2338644720?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=love-hate-relationships">love-hate-relationships</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2338644720" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1051843369378160758"><b>I want to join Zélie and Amari’s squad badly.</b><br/><br/>When you’re a university student, it’s very hard to finish a 500-page book in less than two days and not be five assignments behind, especially this close to the end of the semester. <br/><br/>But here we are, with me still alive and breathing and on track, as impossible as this may seem. I have to thank the author for making this a fast-paced story that does not include a guessing game in every new chapter – otherwise I wouldn’t have been able to read this one</span>
  <span id="freeText1051843369378160758" style="display:none"><b>I want to join Zélie and Amari’s squad badly.</b><br /><br />When you’re a university student, it’s very hard to finish a 500-page book in less than two days and not be five assignments behind, especially this close to the end of the semester. <br /><br />But here we are, with me still alive and breathing and on track, as impossible as this may seem. I have to thank the author for making this a fast-paced story that does not include a guessing game in every new chapter – otherwise I wouldn’t have been able to read this one on the bus and between classes.<br /><br />Surprisingly enough, <i>Children of Blood and Bone</i> is one of those impressive stories that the more you read, the more important it becomes to you. It’s also one that has an intense progression, so much that when you look back at the first chapter, it’s as though you are in another story entirely. <br /><br />This also means that the characters warm up to you gradually – they are not ones that you can automatically imagine yourself being best friends with. Even now, I admire Zélie and Amari profoundly, but I do wonder what we would talk about in real life, seeing that the girls’ minds are almost entirely on the issues to be solved. They do not discuss trivial matters, between themselves or with other characters, thus contributing to the sober atmosphere of the tale. But if I were in this world, I would do everything in my means to be part of their group. Together, they can truly move mountains.<br /><br />The writing does, however, pull you in in a matter of seconds. It’s very focused on describing the actions and emotions of the protagonists from the first person point of view but without overdramatizing the situation. Getting inside the characters’ heads is important because they not only have to deal with external battles, they must extinguish internal ones, too, at times.<br /><br />And since you’re dying to know why I dared take off a star, it’s simple enough: The magic in this world disappeared eleven years ago. I didn’t think it would make a difference if it disappeared a year ago or a hundred years ago, but the protagonists remembering what it was like to have magic made me feel like I wasn’t one hundred percent in sync with them. Not only that, but it would have been more powerful if Zélie had discovered magic after centuries of not having it around.<br /><br />But it really is an astounding debut novel. After that ending, I am all the more intrigued to see where this series goes. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1051843369378160758" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2181516345" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2181516345" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2181516345?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=signed">signed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2181516345" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11865363878017934619"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1522533935i/25303306._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>ARC provided by the publisher via Netgalley in exchange for an honest review.</i><br/><br/>Buddy read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/15079473-adri' rel='nofollow noopener'>Adri</a>! 🦊<br/><br/>(And my favorite BookTube reviews: <a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=J1A28oVjGnQ' rel='nofollow noopener'>Frankie's</a>, <a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=SKnOSgTOOVk' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tati's</a>, & <a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ewUEJFzCb4g' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lauren's</a>!)<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You crushed us to build your monarchy on the backs of our blood and bone. Your mistake wasn’t keeping us alive. It was thinking we’d never fight back!”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><i>Children of Blood and Bone</i> is worth every ounce of hype and praise it has received thus far, and I only anticipate it to receive more and more, especially since you’re al</span>
  <span id="freeText11865363878017934619" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1522533935i/25303306._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>ARC provided by the publisher via Netgalley in exchange for an honest review.</i><br><br>Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/15079473-adri" rel="nofollow noopener">Adri</a>! 🦊<br><br>(And my favorite BookTube reviews: <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=J1A28oVjGnQ" rel="nofollow noopener">Frankie's</a>, <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=SKnOSgTOOVk" rel="nofollow noopener">Tati's</a>, &amp; <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ewUEJFzCb4g" rel="nofollow noopener">Lauren's</a>!)<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You crushed us to build your monarchy on the backs of our blood and bone. Your mistake wasn’t keeping us alive. It was thinking we’d never fight back!”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><i>Children of Blood and Bone</i> is worth every ounce of hype and praise it has received thus far, and I only anticipate it to receive more and more, especially since you’re all about to read a gush review for it. The world is amazing, the characters are so real feeling, the writing is perfect, the action is abundant, the romances are beautiful, the topics are important. This was such a fantastic read, and even though it is only late January, I have no doubts that <i>Children of Blood and Bone</i> will make my best of 2018 list, and I wouldn’t be surprised if it even takes the number one spot come December 31st. I’m also honored to say that this is the very first book I’ve given five stars to in 2018. <br><br>In this world of Orïsha, magic used to thrive and be celebrated. Our main protagonist, Zélie, remembers this time and what a powerful Divîner her mother was. But she also remembers the way her mother’s body looked, when it was left on display the day that magic died. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I think about the way her corpse hung from that tree. I think about the king who took her away.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Now, the king of Orïsha wants to make sure magic is kept dead, while also keeping all the Divîners that live in Orïsha oppressed. The king ensures that the Divîners are reminded they are lesser, in hopes that they will forget how powerful they once were, along with everyone else. And this has worked, for the last eleven years, that is until a powerful artifact is found and if it is combined with a couple other powerful artifacts it can bring magic back to Orïsha once and for all. <br><br>When a Maji is born with white hair, it is a sign that they are touched by the Gods, so they are called Divîners. And back before magic disappeared, when a Divîner turned thirteen, they would develop what kind of power they had from whatever God had touched them. The powers range from healing, to taming animals, to wielding light, to controlling time, to making fire, to calling water, to controlling people’s minds and dreams, to even more things! They were very powerful, and the ordinary people didn’t like them being that powerful, so they had to shut them down and keep them down. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“No matter how much I crave peace, the gods have other plans.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>This story truly focuses on two sets of siblings. One set is Zélie and her brother Tzain, who are currently living in Eloirin, which is surrounded by water, with their father. Yet, the people in Eloirin are forced to pay a Divîner tax, and the prince keeps raising them higher and higher. And if you can’t pay it, then you are forced to perform hard labor (or other worse things) until your debt is paid off. But that’s the thing, you’ll just accumulate more and more debt, and you will never be free again. You will die a slave. And Zélie ‘s family is unsure how they are going to afford to pay the tax for her, so they are forced to go to the city of Lagose to trade. Then, Zélie and Tzain’s story mixes with the other sibling’s story by pure fate of the Gods. <br><br>Amari is the daughter of the king that has done everything to destroy magic. Yet, this princess is nothing like her tyrant of a father. And once her father does something completely unthinkable and totally heartless, Amari flees her royal life once and for all. <br><br>Inan is the king in waiting and Amari’s older brother. He is probably the most interesting character in this book, because he constantly is struggling between what he wants to be and what has always been forced upon him. And he is tasked to bring Amari back to their king of a father, by whatever means necessary. Then, these four young adults, from very different upbringings, come together to change the fate of Orïsha forever. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“They built this world for you, built it to love you. They never cursed at you in the streets, never broke down the doors of your home. They didn’t drag your mother by her neck and hang her for the whole world to see.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>This story is truly unforgettable, and I loved it more than any words I can string together to form a review. The world building is expertly done, and perfectly interwoven through the story. The magic system is so unique and was an absolute joy to learn and read about. Zélie is everything I want in a main protagonist, and her castmates are nothing short of amazing, too. This book was everything I’ve ever wanted from the fantasy genre.<br><br>The writing in this is so very lyrical. I was completely blown away by the magnificent prose. This story is just told so beautifully, I think it would be hard not to fall in love with it. And I want to emphasize that romance is never at the forefront of this story, but some of the one liners that Tomi Adeyemi gave me where truly some of the most romantic lines I’ve ever read. I can’t believe this is her debut novel. Please, just give her all the awards now, because her writing is truly on another level. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You have your duty and your heart. To choose one means the other must suffer.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>And the messages and parallels to our world, from systemic racism, to prison systems, to so much more, are so very important. I know this is a YA high fantasy novel, but I hope people can’t miss the similarities to the very society we are living in today. <br><br>And every single character in this book is beautifully black. Yet, the author does such a wonderful job touching on how people perceive darker skinned individuals to lighter skinned individuals in this world. In this world, the royals want to look as light as possible. Even going as far as to make sure their skin is always powdered, and it is shunned to spend too much time outside where you could become darker. Yet, this young girl, Zélie, with the darkest skin, living in poverty and dealing with the brutal murder of her mother, could be the most powerful person in Orïsha, yet she is viewed as nothing more than a racial slur. This book is powerful, eye opening, and I hope you all take more out of it besides it being an amazing, five starred story. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I won’t let your ignorance silence my pain.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>This book was a masterpiece. Again, I know with my whole soul that this book will make my best of 2018 list without question. I loved this book with the sum of my being and I know it is going to make so many other’s lists, too. Tomi Adeyemi will forever and always be an auto-buy author for me, because this is maybe the strongest debut novel I have ever read in my entire life. Perfection. <br><br><b>Trigger/Content warnings</b> for attempted rape, physical abuse, death, gore, murder, torture, war themes, and similar things in that vein. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“The truth cuts like the sharpest knife I’ve ever known. No matter what I do, I will always be afraid.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a> <br><br><i>The quotes above were taken from an ARC and are subject to change upon publication.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="11865363878017934619" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2352325521" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2352325521" />
    <a title="Sade" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16037420-sade"><img alt="Sade" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605390492p2/16037420.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2352325521?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sade" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sade" href="/user/show/16037420-sade">Sade</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2352325521" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1775227175845081481"><p><br/><b><i>A thoroughly dissappointing read. </i></b><br/>Before i dive into this review, i'd just like to say that i did like the premise of this book. I liked the fact that Tomi wanted to explore Yoruba mythology, i also absolutely loved the fact that she wanted to put Nigeria not just as a place representing Africa as a whole but a country with it's unique culture and all that - she failed in that though , but hey at least she didn't do the whole Africa is a country thing.<br/><br/>First of: Adeyemi had a chance really to pro</p></span>
  <span id="freeText1775227175845081481" style="display:none"><p><br /><b><i>A thoroughly dissappointing read. </i></b><br />Before i dive into this review, i'd just like to say that i did like the premise of this book. I liked the fact that Tomi wanted to explore Yoruba mythology, i also absolutely loved the fact that she wanted to put Nigeria not just as a place representing Africa as a whole but a country with it's unique culture and all that - she failed in that though , but hey at least she didn't do the whole Africa is a country thing.<br /><br />First of: Adeyemi had a chance really to properly explore yoruba mythology and you know just educate people but somewhere along the line everything started looking like a rebooted Netflix Version of your fave animie. How do you delete Olodumare, Olorun and Olofi and put Sky Mother??? Who is that? <br /><br />Then this Nigeria depicted in this book is so lazy. I know, i know, people might say it's fiction but Nigeria is a real ass place. The least you can if you're going to use real places and basically base the identity of your characters as Nigerians is to actually <b>PROPERLY</b> represent such a country. First of Nigeria is freaking huge. So when these characters were hot steping from Lagos - Ilorin - Sokoto in a matter of days i'm sorry i just couldn't roll with it. Then the weather, i mean c'mon snow in Ibadan??? Look i never saw snow until i lived outside Nigeria for 2 years. So this thing she does where she sort of uses weak token gestures to make these characters believable Nigerians is sad. I mean what is with this dashikis they were wearing? I didn't even see one mention of an Agbada or a fila or something. <br /><br />Now that i think about it, you're not even sure what era in Nigeria she's basing her characterisation of Nigeria on. I'm saying this because 1. she mentions Gombe State. Gombe was created in 1996 out of Bauchi State. Also, the author makes it seem like it's just Yoruba that exists in the whole of Nigeria. I find it difficult to imagine for example that people in Sokoto are going to care one hoot for a yoruba deity. Nigeria has so many tribes who i'm sure obviously have their own mythologies and the author basically saying the whole Nigeria is yoruba is just like i said, a lazy depiction of Nigeria.<br /><br />Then the hair. See. I've noticed authors want to write in black women/girls but never want to write them with real hair. HOW WERE ZELIE &amp; AMARI'S HAIR BONE STRAIGHT? Did they have relaxers? Binta's hair is literally described as falling in silky sheets. I mean how??? Inan describes Zelie hair like this "White locks that once fell in smooth sheets now cascade down her back in flowing waves" Ugh!!!! Forget the mushy description. But even when her hair is going natural, Tomi Adeyemi still refuses to give her the typical hair you would find on an average Nigerian girl. I mean except she had Fulani blood in her which she clearly didn't, This hair thing was a huge fail. <br /> <b>Could be wrong, but i honestly feel like she was pandering to her non African audience in terms of the hair &amp; depiction of Nigeria. Which is why her characters for me almost feel like foreign Nigerians. I mean even the name of her main character is so not Yoruba. Fun fact: There's no 'z' in the yoruba alphabet so where did the name Zelie come from?</b><br /><br />Let's dive into the plot proper...Which is frankly a hot mess. The magic system is completely unexplained which i felt was delibrately done in order to carry Inan's story arc. Then blood magic?? Really if anyone knows what that was all about, feel free to explain it to me please.<br />The constant need YA authors have to pair characters up like if that doesn't happen, the whole plot will spontaneously combust. The annoying, irritating fact that even though this author is a woman she couldn't make Zelie bad ass enough and stop being so damn emotional. <br /><b><i>We have so few bad ass female MC's, and the few YA authors manage to write, have their abilities forever overshadowed by falling in love with some freaking dramatic shit of a male character that cannot get his priorities right. </i></b><br />Also whoa!!! The Avatar Last Airbender similarites were so glaring that i was unable to unsee them at every freaking point. <br /><br /><i><b>I honestly feel the bar is basically set on the floor for YA novels, which is why someone can toss in a few Yoruba words, add a real African country in it for good measure, have a gaping plot hole in terms of the magic system, give characters magic willy nilly but still have everyone go awwww because hey guess what, i know i didn't tell you how it works but don't worry here's two beautiful characters falling in love don't stress yourself on how everything works. You want to know the deal with Blood magic? shhh shhhh here's two beautiful characters kissing.</b></i><br /><br /> <i><b><blockquote>Miss me with this book!</blockquote> </b></i><br /></p></span>
  <a data-text-id="1775227175845081481" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2408326201" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2408326201" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2408326201?book_show_action=true">Dec 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=ya-series">ya-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2408326201" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1625052056752189487"><blockquote>
<img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1577566310i/28681238._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Psst. A new video is up - all about the bad books I've read this year! <br/><br/>Now that you know that this one is on it, check out the <b><u><a href='https://youtu.be/c3HUZPHWlPg' rel='nofollow noopener'>Worst Books of 2019 video</a></u></b> to see what other ones made the cut! </blockquote><b>Here's the written review</b><blockquote>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1589141522i/29451023._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  <br/>
  <br/>
  <i>I won't let your ignorance silence my pain</i>
</blockquote>*cue me tearing my hair out*<br/><br/>Okay, so I saw a lot (and I mean a LOT) of positive reviews for this one on Goodreads, so I absolutely could not wait to pick it up.<br/><br/>The reviewers were raving, the cover was gorgeous, the blurb promised</span>
  <span id="freeText1625052056752189487" style="display:none"><blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1577566310i/28681238._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Psst. A new video is up - all about the bad books I've read this year! <br><br>Now that you know that this one is on it, check out the <b><u><a href="https://youtu.be/c3HUZPHWlPg" rel="nofollow noopener">Worst Books of 2019 video</a></u></b> to see what other ones made the cut! </blockquote><b>Here's the written review</b><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1589141522i/29451023._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>
  <br>
  <i>I won't let your ignorance silence my pain</i>
</blockquote>*cue me tearing my hair out*<br><br>Okay, so I saw a lot (and I mean a LOT) of positive reviews for this one on Goodreads, so I absolutely could not wait to pick it up.<br><br>The reviewers were raving, the cover was gorgeous, the blurb promised the world...and what did I get? <br><br><b>A blender full of massacred YA tropes. </b><blockquote>
  <i>Courage does not always roar. Valor does not always shine.</i>
</blockquote>(Come on, admit it - there's at least 10 YA books who have use quotes like that). <br><br>Before I fully go off on this one, there were <b>a few things I liked. </b><br><br>1) The scenery and setting was really well done. I loved the descriptions of the lands and all the details that brought the smaller moments to life. It helped immerse me into this world so different from my own.<br><br>(<b>BUT NOTICE</b> - how my favorite thing about the book is the scenery. The scenery! It's never good when the background is the best part of your book!)<br><br>2) I also loved the concept - the whole rise up against the racism and oppression of the magic folks. Combine that with the setting, and I was so intrigued by how the book was going to turn out.<br><br>(<b>BUT NOTICE</b> - that the overall theme is rising up against racism and oppression...it's not particularly unique in the YA world, is it?)<br><br>That being said, I was still rather excited when I finally got my hands on it. <br><br>And what was served to me? <b>Petty squabbles and predictable plots.</b><br><br><b>Petty Squabbles and Other General Annoyances</b><blockquote>
  <i>You’re always screwing things up. Why stop now?</i>
</blockquote>One of my greatest pet peeves is when banter becomes arguments. I love a good exchange of wits, but that often requires...wit. <br><br>They just felt like childish caricatures of YA characters. They each seemed to have a few phrases that were repeated ad nauseam throughout the book. <blockquote>
  <i>I let out a breath I didn’t know I was holding.</i>
</blockquote> Come on, really? <br><br>First of all, how often can that physically happen to someone without them passing out at least once? Second of all, that phrase...ugh. How did the editors let her get away with that cliche phrase? <br><br>In addition, the love felt very weak to me. <blockquote>
  <i>Love is too strong, too intense, for what I feel. For what I am allowed to feel.</i>
</blockquote>Combine that with the fact that it happened over the course of hours...ugh. <br><br>It just felt so over the top that <b>I honestly didn't have the energy to care</b>...and once that happens, it becomes very hard for me to enjoy the book.<br><br><b>Predictable Plots</b><blockquote>
  <i>They don't hate you, my child. They hate what you were meant to become.</i>
</blockquote>Destiny, limited timeline, find your true love....yadda yadda yadda.<br><br>Let it be known that I am <b>NOT</b> good at predicting books. I'm terrible.<br><br>When I was reading the Harry Potter books, I went into each book fully expecting Harry to die. (Mind you, I was like 12...but still, you'd think that I would've picked up on how the series is named after him, and killing him off in the third one wouldn't make sense).<br><br>So, if I (of all people) can figure out where you are taking the book, then there's a problem. <br><br>I wouldn't have minded so much if it was just here and there. It was just constant. <br><br>The characters decide to do something, I have a little prediction pop up in my head, and then BOOM, that same thing happens. For 500+ pages. <br><br>And it's not just general plot progress. <br><br>The character's development, actions and decisions all felt very choreographed.<br><br> There wasn't much (if anything) that surprised me throughout the book...which made the 500 pages feel so. dang. long.<br><br><b>Overall</b><br><br>I don't know, maybe I just had a bad day with this one but I honestly don't think I can keep going with this series. I'm done. I'm out. <br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads</span>
  <a data-text-id="1625052056752189487" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
